--- Commit Message ---
LU-13805 llite: add mm to dio struct

When copying to or from userspace, we must use the mm from
the userspace thread.  This can be done either by running
in that thread or borrowing its mm.  Unaligned DIO does
some memory movement to userspace in ptlrpcd threads, so it
requires the user mm be stored in the sub dio.

This will be used by the main unaligned DIO patch and has
been split out for reviewability.

Signed-off-by: Patrick Farrell <pfarrell@whamcloud.com>

--- Message (Oleg Drokin, 2023-08-20 17:17:45.000000000) ---
Patch Set 29: Code-Review-1

(1 comment)

can't introduce ssleeping under spinlock

--- Message (Patrick Farrell, 2023-08-20 18:32:20.000000000) ---
Patch Set 29:

So there appear to be two things here, which may be related.

Scheduling while atomic, and spinlock badness.

The scheduling while atomic is coming from ptlrpc_check_set, which is an existing problem - we call ptlrpc_check_set as part of a condition check on an event wait, and it can sleep.  RHEL 8 shouts about this in other contexts.

The spinlock badness - no idea.  Not clear to me how the scheduling in atomic could cause that, but perhaps?  Which is especially interesting because I'm pretty sure I haven't seen it in other runs with Janitor for the patches based on this one.  Either of these, actually.

I will dig around.

OK.  Well, we have an existing issue in ptlrpc_check_set() which comes up on RHEL8, which is perhaps a slightly different issue but it's related to atomic context - we discussed it at LUG.  I'd have to look again at Janitor testing on RHEL8 to find it, but it's related to things we do ptlrpc_check_set() when we're in an inappropriate TASK_ state.

But I can't see any spinlock we're under here, though.

Here's the check in __might_resched - this is from upstream, so it might be different on RHEL 7, but:
-----------
void __might_resched(const char *file, int line, unsigned int offsets)
{
	/* Ratelimiting timestamp: */
	static unsigned long prev_jiffy;

	unsigned long preempt_disable_ip;

	/* WARN_ON_ONCE() by default, no rate limit required: */
	rcu_sleep_check();

	if ((resched_offsets_ok(offsets) && !irqs_disabled() &&
	     !is_idle_task(current) && !current->non_block_count) ||
	    system_state == SYSTEM_BOOTING || system_state > SYSTEM_RUNNING ||
	    oops_in_progress)
		return;
----------------
That "is_idle_task" is what bites us on RHEL 8.  But I'm thinking that check isn't there on RHEL 7.

But if it's not that, do you have any idea what spinlock we're under?  I'm not seeing anything.

Also, by the way, you said this was ignored - I did miss it.  It's hard to notice test-specific failures right now because the failure rate on full Janitor testing is ~100%.

Well, it was a not a "test failure", it was a "new warning".

Those have very low false positive rates.

rhel8 issue is different too, that one is about wrong task state at sleep time - something that rhel7.x don't test for yet.
